EVOLUTION ANSWER:
**1. EARLY POSITION:**
In the early period, climate rhetoric was present in two main contexts: local advocacy and general policy support. Climate groups were noted for their efforts "to advocate and educate" locally, linking the issue to the region's "natural surroundings." Additionally, policy documents encouraged U.S. support for "environmental change" within broader strategies, such as the Strategy for Pacific Partnership.

**2. LATE POSITION:**
In the late period, climate rhetoric expanded significantly to include strong moral, economic, and national security dimensions. Climate change and environmental destruction were explicitly labeled a "sin against God's creation" by religious leaders. Furthermore, the need for clean energy was framed as a matter of "economic security" and "national security," with the Department of Defense considering climate change to be a "top national securit[y]" issue.

**3. THE EVOLUTION:**
The rhetoric evolved from focusing on local advocacy and general environmental support within international aid frameworks to incorporating high-level concerns regarding **national security, economic stability, and moral/religious condemnation**. The change reflects a clear trend toward integrating climate change into core defense and security policy discussions, elevating the issue from a general environmental concern to a critical threat to national interests.

EVOLUTION ANSWER:
**1. EARLY POSITION:**
During the early period, climate and environmental issues were discussed primarily in two contexts: as a general area for U.S. support in foreign policy (facilitating support for "environmental change" in the Pacific Islands) and as a topic for local advocacy and education ("climate groups to advocate and educate"), often linked to the importance of natural surroundings.

**2. LATE POSITION:**
In the late period, the rhetoric surrounding climate change became significantly more urgent and broad. Climate change was explicitly framed as a "top national security" concern (as viewed by the Department of Defense), an issue of economic necessity requiring "homegrown clean and sustainable energy," and a moral/religious imperative, having been called "a sin against God's creation."

**3. THE EVOLUTION:**
The rhetoric shows a clear trend toward increased urgency and a broader scope of concern. The discussion shifted from treating climate as a general area for support or a topic for local advocacy to framing it as a critical, high-level threat that impacts **national security, economic stability, and moral/religious values.** The late documents elevate climate change from an environmental issue to a core national and moral crisis.

EVOLUTION ANSWER:
1. EARLY POSITION:
The early documents discuss various aspects of security, including energy security, AI security, social security, and national security threats. While general budget discussions are mentioned (such as cuts to the arts budget or a £33 million deferral to the Scottish Government), the documents do not provide a specific monetary figure allocated to security for 2024.

2. LATE POSITION:
The late documents continue to address different security domains, including food security, national security, and the security of the Legal Aid Agency’s systems. One document mentions the announcement of the "biggest sustained increase in defence spending since the cold war," but a specific monetary budget allocated to security in 2024 is not detailed.

3. THE EVOLUTION:
The specific budget allocated to security in 2024 is not provided in either the early or late documents. Positions remained stable in that both periods focused on the importance of various security domains and discussed general budget allocations or increases in defense spending, but the requested specific monetary figure is absent.

EVOLUTION ANSWER:
1. EARLY POSITION:
The official position during the early period was focused on reacting to specific conflict events in the region. This included acknowledging an "inexcusable terror attack on Israelis" and assessing the implications of "recent increases in violence in the west bank" for government policies.

2. LATE POSITION:
The provided documents from the late period do not contain any mention of the State of Israel, Israelis, or related geopolitical conflicts. Therefore, the official position during the late period cannot be determined from the available text.

3. THE EVOLUTION:
The topic of the State of Israel and related conflicts was present in the early period documents, primarily in reaction to violence and terror attacks. However, this topic is entirely absent from the late period documents. Consequently, there is no information available to determine if the official position regarding the State of Israel changed or remained stable.

EVOLUTION ANSWER:
**1. EARLY POSITION:**
The official position regarding Hamas or Gaza cannot be determined from the provided early period documents, as this topic is not mentioned. The documents focus on issues such as water company performance, sanitary bins legislation, support for Ukraine, NATO membership, and inflation.

**2. LATE POSITION:**
The official position regarding Hamas or Gaza cannot be determined from the provided late period documents, as this topic is not mentioned. The documents focus on issues such as reducing reoffending, prison officer schemes, cyber-security support for Ukraine, and critical national infrastructure security.

**3. THE EVOLUTION:**
No information is available to determine the evolution of the official position regarding Hamas or Gaza, as the topic is absent from both the early and late period documents. The position remained stable in its absence from the provided text.

EVOLUTION ANSWER:
1. EARLY POSITION:
The early documents do not detail the official position regarding support for the State of Israel. However, they indicate that the government was paying close attention to "concerning figures" produced by the Home Office and the Community Security Trust regarding levels of antisemitism in the preceding 12 months.

2. LATE POSITION:
The late documents confirm that the Government was "in regular contact with all those involved in negotiations," including the Foreign Secretary, who spoke to his "Israeli counterpart last week" (in the context of a discussion dated April 2025). The documents do not explicitly state whether the official position was supportive of the State of Israel during this period, nor do they specifically address the last quarter of 2023.

3. THE EVOLUTION:
The documents do not provide sufficient information to track an evolution in the official position regarding support for the State of Israel. The early period focused on domestic concerns about antisemitism, while the later period confirmed high-level diplomatic contact with the "Israeli counterpart." A clear trend or stable position regarding support for the State of Israel cannot be determined from the provided texts, and the specific position for the last quarter of 2023 is not mentioned.

EVOLUTION ANSWER:
1. EARLY POSITION:
The documents covering the early period, including those dated in the last quarter of 2023 (November 29 and December 13), do not contain any statements or discussions regarding the official position on Hamas or Gaza. Topics addressed include Prime Minister’s engagements, the Holocaust Memorial Bill, water company finances, trade, and an escaped terror suspect.

The documents covering the late period do not contain any statements or discussions regarding the official position on Hamas or Gaza. Topics addressed include Labour’s clean energy plans, obligations to Afghans, NATO commitments, and support for Ukraine.

3. THE EVOLUTION:
There is no discernible evolution or change in the official position regarding support for Hamas or Gaza, as this specific topic is not addressed in any of the provided documents across either the early or late periods. The position remained stable in that it was not mentioned.

EVOLUTION ANSWER:
**1. EARLY POSITION:**

During the early period, the official position was characterized by stability in certain regulatory areas and commitment to existing frameworks:

*   **Drug Testing:** The position on drug testing providers had "not changed," requiring them to have a license to test for controlled drugs (ID hierarchical\_bm25\_82).
*   **International Law:** The Prime Minister was committed to a plan that ensured all steps would be taken to stay within international law (ID hierarchical\_bm25\_2323).
*   **Ministerial Status:** Following an emergency reshuffle, there was a temporary lack of a disabilities Minister (ID hierarchical\_bm25\_2420).

**2. LATE POSITION:**

During the late period, the documents indicate potential shifts in policy and a change in the underlying rationale for government action:

*   **Asylum Seeker Housing:** There was an indication that the position on using large sites to house asylum seekers "may have changed" under the new Government Front Bench team, contrasting with the previous ministerial team's desire to stop their use (ID hierarchical\_bm25\_13370).
*   **Economic Philosophy:** The Prime Minister repeatedly stated that "the world has changed," suggesting a shift in outlook that necessitates government intervention to support domestic production (ID hierarchical\_bm25\_10570).
*   **Defense:** The Government maintained a commitment made at NATO (ID hierarchical\_bm25\_12285).

**3. THE EVOLUTION:**

The official position shows evidence of change, particularly following the introduction of a new ministerial team and a stated shift in global perspective.

*   **Policy Shift:** While the early period emphasized stability in specific regulations (drug testing), the late period explicitly notes a potential change in policy regarding the use of large sites for housing asylum seekers (ID hierarchical\_bm25\_13370).
*   **Philosophical Shift:** The Prime Minister moved from a focus on commitment to existing international law (Early Period) to asserting that "the world has changed" (Late Period), which is used as justification for intervening to support domestic production (ID hierarchical\_bm25\_10570).
*   **Trend:** The documents suggest that positions did **not remain stable** across all sectors, with specific policies being reviewed or altered following ministerial changes and a broader reassessment of the global economic environment.

EVOLUTION ANSWER:
**1. EARLY POSITION:**
The early position directly addressed the conflict in the Middle East, characterizing it as an unfolding "tragedy." The rhetoric acknowledged that "Israel has suffered the worst terror attack in its history" while simultaneously noting that "Palestinian civilians are experiencing a devastating and growing humanitarian crisis." The focus was on supporting steps, such as a recent agreement, that were "a crucial step towards providing relief."

**2. LATE POSITION:**
The late position contains no direct rhetoric regarding the war between Israel and Hamas/Gaza. The Prime Minister/President’s focus in the late period documents is overwhelmingly on the war in Ukraine (discussing President Zelensky, Russia’s illegal invasion, and diplomatic efforts in Washington and London) and domestic issues (such as welfare reform and environmental concerns).

**3. THE EVOLUTION:**
The rhetoric regarding the Israel/Hamas/Gaza conflict did not change in tone but rather disappeared entirely from the provided documents. The early period featured explicit statements balancing support for Israel following the terror attack with concern for the humanitarian crisis in Gaza. The late period shows a clear shift in focus, with the Prime Minister/President’s attention and rhetoric centered on the war in Ukraine and related defense and security matters, indicating that the Middle East conflict was no longer a primary topic of discussion in these later speeches.

The specific identity (name) of the Minister of Defense/Secretary of Defense remains unknown throughout both periods. The position was not explicitly identified in the early period documents. In the late period, while the name is still absent, there is an indication that the Secretary of State responsible for defence spending is female ("she").

EVOLUTION ANSWER:
1. EARLY POSITION:
During the early period (2023), immigration policy was highly contentious and unstable. Documents refer to the "unfixable Rwanda policy" and internal pressure from the Immigration Minister, who was reportedly instructing the Prime Minister to "tear up all our legal obligations" to fix the policy. There was also discussion about launching an "entirely different Conservative immigration policy," indicating that significant, potentially stricter, changes were being sought or debated.

2. LATE POSITION:
The provided documents from the late period (2025) do not contain any information regarding immigration policy, its status, or its strictness.

3. THE EVOLUTION:
It is impossible to determine if immigration policy was stricter in 2025 than in 2023 based solely on the provided documents. While the early period showed a clear intent and pressure to move towards radical, potentially stricter, policy changes (such as abandoning legal obligations related to the Rwanda policy), the late period documents offer no evidence of whether these changes were implemented or what the final policy status was. The trend is **undocumented** in the late period.

EVOLUTION ANSWER:
1. EARLY POSITION:
During the early period, climate change was framed as a major global challenge that required leadership from democracies, such as the UK, and was linked to issues like development, failed regimes, and the growing number of asylum seekers. Rhetoric highlighted that the private sector was being "held back" by "weak policy signals, uncertainty, and barriers to investment," suggesting a need for clearer policy direction to unlock investment and reduce reliance on other nations. Climate change was also recognized as a "major obstacle to eliminating extreme poverty."

2. LATE POSITION:
In the late period, the rhetoric emphasized the immediate, widespread impact of climate change, stating that "Tackling climate change should matter to all of us because it affects all of us." The focus shifted heavily toward implementation, urgency, and specific technical targets. This included stressing the need for carbon removal (10 billion tonnes annually by 2050) to meet the 1.5° target, tracking progress against "strong climate targets" set at COP29, and addressing domestic impacts, such as coastal erosion which is "only set to get worse." Furthermore, policy discussion focused on practical steps like ensuring "cheaper electricity" so households can transition away from gas heating.

3. THE EVOLUTION:
The rhetoric evolved from identifying climate change as a major global challenge requiring stronger policy signals (Early Position) to focusing on the *urgency of implementation* and the *specific domestic and technical requirements* needed to meet established targets (Late Position). While the early period noted the need to address "weak policy signals," the late period focused on the UK leading the way on "strong climate targets" (COP29) and the necessity of specific measures like carbon removal and ensuring affordable household transitions (cheaper electricity). The late rhetoric also explicitly linked climate change to the worsening of specific domestic problems, such as coastal erosion. The overall trend shows a shift from broad recognition and policy critique toward detailed implementation and urgent action based on scientific targets.

EVOLUTION ANSWER:
1. EARLY POSITION:
The early documents discuss various aspects of security, including antisemitism, national security threats from China, energy security, cyber security, and social security changes. While general budget discussions are present (e.g., cuts to the arts budget or a £33 million grant to the Scottish Government), the specific monetary budget allocated to security for 2024 is not mentioned.

2. LATE POSITION:
The late documents continue to address security issues, such as food security, national security, and bolstering the security of the Legal Aid Agency’s systems. Although one document mentions the announcement of the "biggest sustained increase in defence spending since the cold war," the specific monetary figure allocated to the security budget for 2024 is not provided.

3. THE EVOLUTION:
The specific budget allocated to security in 2024 is consistently absent from the provided documents across both periods. Therefore, the data point requested remains stable in its lack of detail. However, there is an evolution in the discussion of related spending, as the late period documents explicitly mention a policy decision to implement the "biggest sustained increase in defence spending since the cold war," indicating a significant commitment to increased expenditure in the defence/security sector, even without providing the exact 2024 figure.

The late period documents indicate that the Government maintained diplomatic contact with the State of Israel. Specifically, the Foreign Secretary spoke to his "Israeli counterpart" (ID: hierarchical_dense_10494). This contact was part of the Government being "in regular contact with all those involved in negotiations" (ID: hierarchical_dense_10494).

The documents do not provide a clear position for the last quarter of 2023 as requested. Based on the provided texts, the position evolved from being unmentioned in the early period to demonstrating active, high-level diplomatic contact with the Israeli counterpart in the late period. The documents confirm diplomatic engagement but do not explicitly detail the nature of official support.

Since the official position on Hamas or Gaza is not discussed in any of the provided documents, it is impossible to identify any change or trend in policy or views between the early and late periods. The documents are silent on this specific foreign policy issue.

EVOLUTION ANSWER:
1. EARLY POSITION:
During the early period, the official position on drug testing providers was stable: they must have a licence to test for controlled drugs, including at festivals, a condition which had "always had that condition in place" [hierarchical_dense_82]. The Prime Minister was committed to a plan that included assurances that all steps would be taken to stay within international law [hierarchical_dense_2323].

2. LATE POSITION:
In the late period, there was an indication that the position regarding the use of large sites to house asylum seekers may have changed, contrasting with the previous ministerial team's stated goal to stop their use [hierarchical_dense_13370]. Furthermore, the Prime Minister maintained the position that the world has changed, witnessing the end of globalisation, which implies the Government must intervene to support domestic production [hierarchical_dense_10570].

3. THE EVOLUTION:
The documents indicate a potential change in policy direction regarding asylum seeker housing, as the late period noted that the previous ministerial team's position (to stop using large sites) "may have changed" [hierarchical_dense_13370]. The late period also introduced a new position regarding the end of globalisation and the resulting need for government intervention [hierarchical_dense_10570]. However, the early period explicitly stated that the position on drug testing licenses had remained stable and "has not changed" [hierarchical_dense_82].

EVOLUTION ANSWER:
1. EARLY POSITION:
During the early period, the Prime Minister’s rhetoric explicitly addressed the conflict in the Middle East, characterizing it as a "tragedy unfolding." The position acknowledged the suffering of both sides: "Israel has suffered the worst terror attack in its history" and "Palestinian civilians are experiencing a devastating and growing humanitarian crisis." The focus was on the need for relief, noting that a recent agreement was a "crucial step towards providing relief" [hierarchical_dense_1928].

2. LATE POSITION:
In the late period documents, there is no mention of the war between Israel and Hamas/Gaza, the Middle East tragedy, or the humanitarian crisis in Gaza. The Prime Minister’s focus in the provided late documents shifted entirely to other geopolitical issues, primarily the conflict in Ukraine (discussing President Zelensky, Russian aggression, and European security) [hierarchical_dense_10082, hierarchical_dense_9585, hierarchical_dense_9621, hierarchical_dense_9604], and domestic issues like illegal immigration and welfare reform [hierarchical_dense_10469, hierarchical_dense_10097].

3. THE EVOLUTION:
The rhetoric regarding the Israel/Hamas/Gaza conflict did not change in tone but rather disappeared entirely from the provided documents. The initial balanced acknowledgment of the tragedy and humanitarian crisis was replaced by an overwhelming focus on the war in Ukraine and related European security matters. This indicates a clear shift in the Prime Minister's immediate rhetorical priorities away from the Middle East conflict.

**3. THE EVOLUTION:**
It is impossible to determine if immigration policy was stricter in 2025 than in 2023 based solely on the provided documents, as the late period documents do not address immigration policy. The early period documents indicate a strong internal push toward increased strictness.

EVOLUTION ANSWER:
**1. EARLY POSITION:**
During the early period, climate policy rhetoric framed climate change as a major, growing global challenge that democracies, particularly the UK, should lead the fight on (hierarchical_dense_905). It was linked explicitly to broader geopolitical issues, such as being a "major obstacle to eliminating extreme poverty" and contributing to the growing number of asylum seekers due to "failed regimes" (hierarchical_dense_1798, hierarchical_dense_905). Domestically, the rhetoric criticized the government for providing "weak policy signals, uncertainty, and barriers to investment," which were holding back the private sector (hierarchical_dense_1033).

**2. LATE POSITION:**
In the late period, the rhetoric emphasized the urgency and universality of the issue, stating that "Tackling climate change should matter to all of us because it affects all of us" (hierarchical_dense_10020). The focus shifted to specific, measurable targets and implementation requirements. This included the necessity of tracking progress against "strong climate targets" set at international forums like COP29 (hierarchical_dense_10020), meeting the 1.5° target by 2050, and the requirement for large-scale technical solutions like removing 10 billion tonnes of carbon annually (hierarchical_dense_10023). Domestically, the rhetoric focused on the urgency of ensuring cheaper electricity to help households transition away from gas heating and addressing specific impacts like coastal erosion, which is "only set to get worse" due to climate change (hierarchical_dense_10039, hierarchical_dense_10169).

**3. THE EVOLUTION:**
The rhetoric evolved from general statements about global leadership and criticism of weak policy signals to a more urgent, specific, and implementation-focused discussion.

The change shows a clear trend toward greater specificity and technical detail:
*   **From General Challenge to Specific Targets:** The discussion moved from identifying climate change as a "growing challenge" (hierarchical_dense_1798) to referencing specific goals (1.5° target) and technical requirements (10 billion tonnes of carbon removal annually) (hierarchical_dense_10023).
*   **From Policy Uncertainty to Tracking Progress:** The early criticism of "weak policy signals" (hierarchical_dense_1033) was replaced by a focus on the necessity of setting "strong climate targets" and ensuring measures are in place to "track progress against our COP commitments" (hierarchical_dense_10020).
*   **Focus on Domestic Transition:** The late rhetoric explicitly linked climate action to domestic policy implementation, such as the urgency of reducing electricity costs for households transitioning away from gas and addressing worsening coastal erosion (hierarchical_dense_10039, hierarchical_dense_10169).

EVOLUTION ANSWER:
1. EARLY POSITION: The documents from the early period (referencing events up to July 2023) do not establish a single, unified "official position" on a major policy issue. Instead, they reflect individual congressional actions such as introducing specific local legislation (requiring the D.C. National Guard Commanding General to reside in D.C.) and offering commendations for individuals, sports teams, and organizations (e.g., the U.S. Small Business Administration, Israel Nitzan, and water quality advocates).

2. LATE POSITION: The documents from the late period also do not establish a single, unified "official position." They consist primarily of individual congressional statements recognizing and honoring constituents for their achievements (e.g., Girl Scouts, military veterans, public servants like the Crawford County Treasurer, and advocates for refugees and immigrants).

3. THE EVOLUTION: There is no discernible change in an "official position" because the provided documents for both periods do not articulate a consistent, unified policy stance on a major issue. The nature of the content remains stable across both periods, consisting overwhelmingly of individual members' extensions of remarks, commendations, and recognitions of local achievements and service.

EVOLUTION ANSWER:
Based solely on the provided documents, it is not possible to identify or explain how the Prime Minister's or President's rhetoric regarding the war between Israel and Hamas/Gaza changed.

1.  **EARLY POSITION:** The documents from the early period do not contain any statements or rhetoric from a Prime Minister or President concerning the war between Israel and Hamas/Gaza. The documents primarily focus on recognizing individuals, veterans, and discussing unrelated foreign policy (e.g., U.S.-Pacific Islands Summit, Bulgarian energy independence).

2.  **LATE POSITION:** The documents from the late period also do not contain any direct statements or rhetoric from a Prime Minister or President concerning the war between Israel and Hamas/Gaza. While one document mentions an attack carried out "for Gaza" and "for Palestine," and another includes a constituent's view affirming the "special relationship between the U.S. and Israel," these are not the direct rhetoric of the Prime Minister or President.

3.  **THE EVOLUTION:** No evolution or change in rhetoric can be identified because the relevant statements from the Prime Minister or President regarding the Israel/Hamas/Gaza conflict are absent in both the early and late period documents. The position remained stable in its absence from the provided record.

**1. EARLY POSITION:**
During the early period, climate change was an active and central topic of policy discussion and legislative focus. The rhetoric framed climate change as a significant threat, necessitating hearings to examine how it "threatens supply chains" and how it is "fueling severe weather events." Policy discussions focused on the science of "extreme event attribution" and the need for "sustainable, climate-smart agricultural practices." There was also rhetoric celebrating dedication to "fighting climate change."

**2. LATE POSITION:**
The late period documents contain no explicit rhetoric regarding climate change, climate policy, extreme weather, or sustainability efforts. The focus of the late documents shifts entirely to other topics, such as advertising contracts, American cinema, historical policy foundations (Heritage Foundation), wireless leadership, civil rights, and community tributes.

**3. THE EVOLUTION:**
The rhetoric regarding climate policy underwent a significant shift from the early to the late period. In the early period, climate change was a prominent and urgent topic, actively discussed in terms of its scientific links to extreme events and its economic impacts (supply chains), requiring active policy responses ("fighting climate change"). In the late period, this rhetoric completely disappeared from the provided documents, indicating a clear trend away from climate change as a publicly discussed topic within this specific set of records.

EVOLUTION ANSWER:
1. EARLY POSITION:
The documents from the early period (mid-2023) show congressional activity focused on recognizing individual and team achievements (e.g., the Mid Valley High School softball team, Willie Ann Huff's 90th birthday, Luzerne County Sports Hall of Fame inductees) and commemorating anniversaries (e.g., the 70th anniversary of the U.S. Small Business Administration). Legislative focus included introducing specific bills, such as the D.C. National Guard Commanding General Residency Act, and promoting national water policy.

2. LATE POSITION:
The documents from the late period (undated) are entirely focused on recognizing and honoring individuals for their service, leadership, and contributions. Examples include congratulating Girl Scouts for extraordinary leadership, recognizing the legacy of Colonel Richard Tucker and WWII Navy Veteran Mr. Milton Hudson, and honoring the service of school district directors and county treasurers.

3. THE EVOLUTION:
The provided documents do not contain dates corresponding to the last quarter of 2023 or the last quarter of 2025, making it impossible to determine if the official position changed over the specified timeframe. Across both periods, the dominant activity recorded is the recognition and commendation of constituents, veterans, and local leaders. Therefore, based solely on the provided texts, the trend remains stable, focusing heavily on honoring individuals and local achievements rather than detailing a shifting national policy position.

EVOLUTION ANSWER:
1. EARLY POSITION:
The provided documents from the early period (2023) do not contain any information regarding the status or strictness of U.S. immigration policy.

2. LATE POSITION:
The provided documents from the late period (2025) do not contain any information regarding the status or strictness of U.S. immigration policy. One document mentions a recommendation to redesignate Nigeria as a Country of Particular Concern (CPC) in June 2025, but this does not describe the overall strictness of general immigration policy.

3. THE EVOLUTION:
It is impossible to determine if immigration policy was stricter in 2025 than in 2023, as the provided documents do not discuss the strictness or status of immigration policy during either period. The positions remained stable in that no relevant policy information was presented.

EVOLUTION ANSWER:
**1. EARLY POSITION:**
During the early period, climate change was a prominent subject of policy discussion and congressional activity. The rhetoric focused on:
*   **Threat Assessment:** Examining how "climate change threatens supply chains" and how it is "fueling severe weather events" (extreme event attribution).
*   **Action and Solutions:** Discussing "sustainable, climate-smart agricultural practices" and celebrating dedication to "fighting climate change" through science and new energy technologies.
*   **Institutional Focus:** Climate change was a specific focus area for subcommittees (e.g., Subcommittee on Oceans, Fisheries, Climate Change) and full committees (Budget, Environment and Public Works).

**2. LATE POSITION:**
The late period documents contain no explicit rhetoric regarding climate change, climate policy, severe weather attribution, or climate-smart practices. The focus of the late documents is on topics such as advertising contracts, American cinema, historical policy foundations, wireless technology, and community tributes.

**3. THE EVOLUTION:**
The rhetoric concerning climate policy underwent a clear shift from being a central, active topic of discussion and legislative concern to being entirely absent from the provided documents. In the early period, climate change was framed as an immediate threat requiring scientific examination and policy solutions (climate-smart agriculture, fighting climate change). In the late period, this specific policy rhetoric disappeared, indicating a change in the documented focus of congressional discourse.
